Task instruction sent to agent 
# Support CockroachDB as a First-Class Database Backend

**Repository:** flipt-io/flipt
**Language:** Go
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

CockroachDB uses the same wire protocol as PostgreSQL, allowing it to work with existing PostgreSQL-compatible drivers. However, Flipt does not recognize CockroachDB as a distinct backend in configuration or database migrations. Flipt's internal logic currently assumes PostgreSQL when using the Postgres driver, which causes issues when targeting CockroachDB without explicit support. This prevents seamless setup and deployment of Flipt with CockroachDB, even though technical compatibility exists.

## Key Components

- Configuration parsing — where database protocol/driver is resolved from config
- Database migration logic — uses `golang-migrate` with driver-specific handling
- SQL driver initialization — where the PostgreSQL driver is selected and configured

## Task

1. Add `cockroachdb` as a supported database protocol in Flipt's configuration schema
2. Enable migrations using the CockroachDB driver in `golang-migrate`
3. Ensure the CockroachDB backend reuses PostgreSQL SQL driver logic where appropriate
4. Add or update configuration validation to accept the new backend
5. Run existing tests to ensure no regressions with PostgreSQL and other backends

## Success Criteria

- `cockroachdb` is accepted as a valid database protocol in configuration
- Migrations run correctly with the CockroachDB driver
- CockroachDB backend shares appropriate SQL logic with the PostgreSQL backend
- Existing database backends (PostgreSQL, MySQL, SQLite) are unaffected
- All existing tests pass

    12→func runMigrations(cfg *config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) error {
    13→	var (
    14→		migrator *analytics.Migrator
    15→		err      error
    16→	)
    17→
    18→	migrator, err = analytics.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
    19→	if err != nil {
    20→		return err
    21→	}
    22→
    23→	defer migrator.Close()
    24→
    25→	if err := migrator.Up(true); err != nil {
    26→		return fmt.Errorf("running migrator %w", err)
    27→	}
    28→
    29→	return nil
    30→}
    31→
    32→func newMigrateCommand() *cobra.Command {
    33→	cmd := &cobra.Command{
    34→		Use:   "migrate",
    35→		Short: "Run pending database migrations",
    36→		RunE: func(cmd *cobra.Command, _ []string) error {
    37→			ctx := cmd.Context()
    38→			logger, cfg, err := buildConfig(ctx)
    39→			if err != nil {
    40→				return err
    41→			}
    42→
    43→			defer func() {
    44→				_ = logger.Sync()
    45→			}()
    46→
    47→			if err := runMigrations(cfg, logger); err != nil {
    48→				return err
    49→			}
    50→
    51→			return nil
    52→		},
    53→	}
    54→
    55→	cmd.Flags().StringVar(&providedConfigFile, "config", "", "path to config file")
    56→	return cmd
    57→}

    40→	}
    41→

    43→		db:       db,
    44→		migrator: mm,

    12→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    13→// an analytics database.
    14→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    15→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    16→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    17→		if err != nil {
    18→			return nil, "", err
    19→		}
    20→
    21→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    22→
    23→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    27→}

    44→		switch t := v.(type) {
    45→		case map[string]any:
    46→			adapt(t)
    47→		case time.Duration:
    48→			m[k] = t.String()
    49→		}
    50→	}
    51→}

package flipt

import "strings"

import "list"

JsonPath: string

#FliptSpec: {
	// flipt-schema-v2
	//
	// Flipt config file is a YAML file defining how to configure the
	// Flipt application.
	@jsonschema(schema="http://json-schema.org/draft/2019-09/schema#")
	version:         "2.0" | *"2.0"
	experimental?:   #experimental
	analytics?:      #analytics
	authentication?: #authentication
	authorization?:  #authorization
	cors?:           #cors
	diagnostics?:    #diagnostics
	evaluation?:     #evaluation
	environments?:   #environments
	storage?:        #storage
	templates?:      #templates
	credentials?:    #credentials
	log?:            #log
	meta?:           #meta
	server?:         #server
	metrics?:        #metrics
	tracing?:        #tracing
	ui?:             #ui
	license?:        #license

     1→# AGENTS
     2→
     3→This file provides guidance to AI Agents when working with code in this repository.
     4→
     5→All of our documentation is at <https://docs.flipt.io>. Weigh the v2 docs heavily when answering questions over the v1 docs.
     6→
     7→## Project Overview
     8→
     9→Flipt v2 is a Git-native feature management platform with a monorepo structure. This is the v2 version with a Git-native architecture.
    10→
    11→- **v1 code**: Located on `main` branch
    12→- **v2 code**: Located on current (`v2`) branch. This is the default branch in the repository.
    13→- **License**: Fair Core License for server, MIT for client code
    14→- **Requirements**: Go 1.25+ and Node.js 18+
    15→
    16→## Project Architecture & Structure
    17→
    18→### Repository Structure
    19→
    20→- `cmd/flipt/` - Main application entry point
    21→- `core/` - Core validation and business logic
    22→- `errors/` - Shared error definitions
    23→- `internal/` - Core application logic (not importable)
    24→  - `cmd/` - Internal command utilities and code generation tools
    25→  - `common/` - Shared types and utilities across internal packages
    26→  - `config/` - Configuration management
    27→  - `containers/` - Container test utilities
    28→  - `coss/` - Commercial open source features (license management, enterprise storage, secrets)
    29→  - `secrets/` - Secret management system with provider interface (OSS file provider, Pro Vault provider)
    30→  - `credentials/` - Credential management for cloud storage and Git authentication
    31→  - `ext/` - Import/export functionality for flags and segments
    32→  - `gateway/` - HTTP gateway implementation
    33→  - `info/` - Version and build information
    34→  - `migrations/` - Database
... (truncated)

    15→// AnalyticsStorageConfig is a collection of configuration option for storage backends.

    21→func (a AnalyticsStorageConfig) String() string {
    22→	// TODO: make this more dynamic if we add more storage options

    25→	}
    26→

    28→		return "prometheus"
    29→	}
    30→	return ""
    31→}

    33→// ClickhouseConfig defines the connection details for connecting Flipt to Clickhouse.

    35→	Enabled bool   `json:"enabled,omitempty" mapstructure:"enabled" yaml:"enabled,omitempty"`
    36→	URL     string `json:"-" mapstructure:"url" yaml:"url,omitempty"`
    37→}
    38→
    39→// Options returns the connection option details for Clickhouse.
    40→func (c ClickhouseConfig) Options() (*clickhouse.Options, error) {
    41→	options, err := clickhouse.ParseDSN(c.URL)
    42→	if err != nil {
    43→		return nil, err
    44→	}
    45→
    46→	return options, nil
    47→}

     1→package analytics
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"database/sql"
     5→	"errors"
     6→
     7→	"github.com/ClickHouse/clickhouse-go/v2"
     8→
     9→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
    10→)
    11→
    12→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    13→// an analytics database.
    14→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    15→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    16→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    17→		if err != nil {
    18→			return nil, "", err
    19→		}
    20→
    21→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    22→
    23→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    27→}
    28→
    29→var (
    30→	stringToDriver = map[string]Driver{
    31→		"clickhouse": Clickhouse,
    32→	}
    33→)
    34→
    35→// Driver represents a database driver
    36→type Driver string
    37→
    38→func (d Driver) String() string {
    39→	return string(d)
    40→}
    41→
    42→func (d Driver) Migrations() string {
    43→	return d.String()
    44→}
    45→

    12→type Timestamp struct {
    13→	*timestamppb.Timestamp
    14→}
    15→
    16→func (t *Timestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    17→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    18→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    19→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    20→			return err
    21→		}
    22→
    23→		t.Timestamp = val
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil
    27→}
    28→
    29→func (t *Timestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    30→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    31→}
    32→
    33→type NullableTimestamp Timestamp
    34→
    35→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    36→	if value == nil {
    37→		return nil
    38→	}
    39→
    40→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    41→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    42→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    43→			return err
    44→		}
    45→
    46→		t.Timestamp = val
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return nil
    50→}
    51→
    52→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    53→	if t.Timestamp == nil {
    54→		return nil, nil
    55→	}
    56→
    57→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    58→}
    59→
    60→type JSONField[T any] struct {
    61→	T T
    62→}
    63→
    64→func (f *JSONField[T]) Scan(v any) error {
    65→	if v == nil {
    66→		return nil
    67→	}
    68→
    69→	var bytes []byte
    70→	switch b := v.(type) {
    71→	case []byte:
    72→		bytes = b
    73→	case string:
    74→		bytes = []byte(b)
    75→	default:
    76→		return fmt.Errorf("unexpected type for data: %T", v)
    77→	}

    29→func migratorHelper(logger *zap.Logger, db *sql.DB, driver Driver, databaseDriver database.Driver) (*Migrator, error) {
    30→	// source migrations from embedded config/migrations package
    31→	// relative to the specific driver
    32→	sourceDriver, err := iofs.New(migrations.FS, driver.Migrations())
    33→	if err != nil {
    34→		return nil, err
    35→	}
    36→
    37→	mm, err := migrate.NewWithInstance("iofs", sourceDriver, driver.Migrations(), databaseDriver)
    38→	if err != nil {
    39→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("creating migrate instance: %w", err)
    40→	}
    41→
    42→	return &Migrator{
    43→		db:       db,
    44→		migrator: mm,
    45→		logger:   logger,
    46→		driver:   driver,
    47→	}, nil
    48→}

     1→# Database Migrations
     2→
     3→This directory contains the database migrations for the v2 version of Flipt.
     4→
     5→We use [golang-migrate](https://github.com/golang-migrate/migrate) to create and manage the migrations.
     6→
     7→Currently the only database supported is Clickhouse for analytics.
     8→
     9→To create a new migration, run the following command:
    10→
    11→```sh
    12→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/{db} <migration_name>
    13→```
    14→
    15→Where `{db}` is the database type, e.g. `clickhouse`, etc.
    16→
    17→Example:
    18→
    19→```sh
    20→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/clickhouse create_table_X
    21→```
    22→

     2→    `timestamp` DateTime('UTC'),

    13→        'FLAG_DISABLED_EVALUATION_REASON' = 2,

    19→    `entity_id` Nullable(String),
    20→    `value` UInt32
    21→)

    58→	})

    62→	}

    65→}

200-usertool_resultRead
     1→package clickhouse
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"context"
     5→	"fmt"
     6→	"strings"
     7→	"time"
     8→
     9→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/server/analytics"
    10→)
    11→
    12→// IncrementFlagEvaluationCounts does a batch insert of flag values from evaluations.
    13→func (c *Client) IncrementFlagEvaluationCounts(ctx context.Context, responses []*analytics.EvaluationResponse) error {
    14→	if len(responses) < 1 {
    15→		return nil
    16→	}
    17→
    18→	valuePlaceHolders := make([]string, 0, len(responses))
    19→	valueArgs := make([]any, 0, len(responses)*10)
    20→
    21→	for _, response := range responses {
    22→		valuePlaceHolders = append(valuePlaceHolders, "(toDateTime(?, 'UTC'),?,?,?,?,?,?,?,?,?,?)")
    23→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.Timestamp.Format(time.DateTime))
    24→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, counterAnalyticsName)
    25→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.EnvironmentKey)
    26→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.NamespaceKey)
    27→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.FlagKey)
    28→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.FlagType)
    29→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.Reason)
    30→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.Match)
    31→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.EvaluationValue)
    32→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, response.EntityId)
    33→		valueArgs = append(valueArgs, 1)
    34→	}
    35→
    36→	//nolint:gosec
    37→	stmt := fmt.Sprintf("INSERT INTO %s VALUES %s", counterAnalyticsTable, strings.Join(valuePlaceHolders, ","))
    38→
    39→	_, err := c.Conn.ExecContext(ctx, stmt, valueArgs...)
    40→	return err
    41→}
    42→

    43→		return nil, err
    44→	}

    46→	mm, err = newMigrator(db, fliptsql.Clickhouse)
    47→	if err != nil {
    48→		return nil, err
    49→	}
    50→
    51→	if err := mm.Up(); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, migrate.ErrNoChange) {
    52→		return nil, err
    53→	}
    54→
    55→	return &Database{
    56→		Container: container,
    57→		DB:        db,
    58→		Driver:    fliptsql.Clickhouse,
    59→

    12→type Timestamp struct {
    13→	*timestamppb.Timestamp
    14→}
    15→
    16→func (t *Timestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    17→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    18→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    19→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    20→			return err
    21→		}
    22→
    23→		t.Timestamp = val
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil
    27→}
    28→
    29→func (t *Timestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    30→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    31→}

    38→	}

    40→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    41→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    42→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    43→			return err
    44→		}
    45→
    46→		t.Timestamp = val
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return nil
    50→}

    52→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    53→	if t.Timestamp == nil {
    54→		return nil, nil
    55→	}
    56→
    57→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    58→}

    61→	T T

    65→	if v == nil {
    66→		return nil
    67→	}
    68→
    69→	var bytes []byte
    70→	switch b := v.(type) {
    71→	case []byte:
    72→		bytes = b
    73→	case string:
    74→		bytes = []byte(b)
    75→	default:
    76→		return fmt.Errorf("unexpected type for data: %T", v)
    77→	}

    12→func runMigrations(cfg *config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) error {
    13→	var (
    14→		migrator *analytics.Migrator
    15→		err      error
    16→	)
    17→
    18→	migrator, err = analytics.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
    19→	if err != nil {
    20→		return err
    21→	}
    22→
    23→	defer migrator.Close()
    24→
    25→	if err := migrator.Up(true); err != nil {
    26→		return fmt.Errorf("running migrator %w", err)
    27→	}
    28→
    29→	return nil
    30→}
    31→
    32→func newMigrateCommand() *cobra.Command {
    33→	cmd := &cobra.Command{
    34→		Use:   "migrate",
    35→		Short: "Run pending database migrations",
    36→		RunE: func(cmd *cobra.Command, _ []string) error {
    37→			ctx := cmd.Context()
    38→			logger, cfg, err := buildConfig(ctx)
    39→			if err != nil {
    40→				return err
    41→			}
    42→
    43→			defer func() {
    44→				_ = logger.Sync()
    45→			}()
    46→
    47→			if err := runMigrations(cfg, logger); err != nil {
    48→				return err
    49→			}
    50→
    51→			return nil
    52→		},
    53→	}
    54→
    55→	cmd.Flags().StringVar(&providedConfigFile, "config", "", "path to config file")
    56→	return cmd
    57→}

     2→(
     3→    `timestamp` DateTime('UTC'),

    40→	}
    41→
    42→	return &Migrator{
    43→		db:       db,
    44→		migrator: mm,
    45→		logger:   logger,
    46→		driver:   driver,
    47→	}, nil
    48→}

    52→		return nil, err
    53→	}

    49→		}

    53→			clickhouseErr = err
    54→			return
    55→		}
    56→
    57→		conn = connection
    58→	})
    59→
    60→	if clickhouseErr != nil {
    61→		return nil, clickhouseErr
    62→	}
    63→
    64→	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
    65→}

    12→type Timestamp struct {
    13→	*timestamppb.Timestamp
    14→}
    15→
    16→func (t *Timestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    17→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    18→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    19→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    20→			return err
    21→		}
    22→
    23→		t.Timestamp = val
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil
    27→}
    28→
    29→func (t *Timestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    30→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    31→}
    32→
    33→type NullableTimestamp Timestamp
    34→
    35→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    36→	if value == nil {
    37→		return nil
    38→	}
    39→
    40→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    41→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    42→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    43→			return err
    44→		}
    45→
    46→		t.Timestamp = val
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return nil
    50→}
    51→
    52→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    53→	if t.Timestamp == nil {
    54→		return nil, nil
    55→	}
    56→
    57→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    58→}
    59→
    60→type JSONField[T any] struct {
    61→	T T
    62→}
    63→
    64→func (f *JSONField[T]) Scan(v any) error {
    65→	if v == nil {
    66→		return nil
    67→	}
    68→
    69→	var bytes []byte
    70→	switch b := v.(type) {
    71→	case []byte:
    72→		bytes = b
    73→	case string:
    74→		bytes = []byte(b)
    75→	default:
    76→		return fmt.Errorf("unexpected type for data: %T", v)
    77→	}

     1→# Database Migrations
     2→
     3→This directory contains the database migrations for the v2 version of Flipt.
     4→
     5→We use [golang-migrate](https://github.com/golang-migrate/migrate) to create and manage the migrations.
     6→
     7→Currently the only database supported is Clickhouse for analytics.
     8→
     9→To create a new migration, run the following command:
    10→
    11→```sh
    12→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/{db} <migration_name>
    13→```
    14→
    15→Where `{db}` is the database type, e.g. `clickhouse`, etc.
    16→
    17→Example:
    18→
    19→```sh
    20→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/clickhouse create_table_X
    21→```
    22→

## Summary of Findings

Based on my thorough search of the Flipt codebase, here's what I found regarding the `FLIPT_ANALYTICS_DATABASE_PROTOCOL` environment variable and the analytics database system:

### 1. **FLIPT_ANALYTICS_DATABASE_PROTOCOL Environment Variable**

**Location**: `/workspace/internal/server/analytics/clickhouse/client_test.go` (lines 25-26)

The variable is **only used in tests** as a guard:
```go
if os.Getenv("FLIPT_ANALYTICS_DATABASE_PROTOCOL") == "" {
    t.Skip("please provide an analytics database protocol to run tests")
}
```

**Current Usage**: It's checked but **NOT actually used to determine database driver selection**. It's merely a flag to skip the test suite if not set.

---

### 2. **How Analytics Storage Determines Which Database Backend to Use**

**Location**: `/workspace/internal/storage/analytics/db.go` (lines 14-27)

The `open()` function determines the database based on **configuration flags**, not environment variables:

```go
func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
        // Use ClickHouse
        clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
        db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
        return db, Clickhouse, nil
    }
    
    return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
}
```

The decision logic is:
- Check `cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled` boolean flag
- If true, connect to ClickHouse
- Otherwise, return error

---

### 3. **Database Protocol/Driver Abstraction**

**Location**: `/workspace/internal/storage/analytics/db.go` (lines 29-48)

The system defines a **`Driver` type** as a string constant:

```go

     1→# CockroachDB Analytics Backend Implementation Plan
     2→
     3→## Context
     4→
     5→Flipt currently supports ClickHouse and Prometheus as analytics storage backends, but not CockroachDB despite its PostgreSQL-compatible wire protocol. The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.
     6→
     7→CockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.
     8→
     9→## Overview
    10→
    11→The implementation involves:
    12→1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`
    13→2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`
    14→3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver
    15→4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB
    16→5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)
    17→6. Updating testing infrastructure
    18→7. Integrating CockroachDB into the gRPC server initialization
    19→
    20→## Files to Modify
    21→
    22→### 1. **Core Driver System** (`internal/storage/analytics/db.go`)
    23→- Add `CockroachDB` constant to the `Driver` type
    24→- Update `stringToDriver` map to include `"cockroachdb": CockroachDB`
    25→- Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB configuration
    26→- Import PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB connections
    27→
    28→### 2. **Configuration** (`internal/config/analytics.go`)

    30→- Add `CockroachDBConfig` field to `AnalyticsStorageConfig`

## Summary of My Implementation Plan

Based on extensive code exploration, I've designed a plan to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend. Here's what will be implemented:

**Key Components:**
1. **Driver System** - Add CockroachDB as a new Driver type alongside ClickHouse
2. **Configuration** - Add CockroachDBConfig struct following the ClickHouse pattern  
3. **Migrations** - Create PostgreSQL-compatible SQL migration files (CockroachDB uses Postgres wire protocol)
4. **Migrator** - Update to use PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for CockroachDB
5. **Configuration Schema** - Add CockroachDB to CUE and JSON schemas
6. **Testing** - Adapt testing infrastructure to support CockroachDB containers
7. **Server Integration** - Add CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server

## Implementation Plan Summary

The plan outlines how to add CockroachDB support to Flipt's analytics layer by:

1. **Adding CockroachDB Driver Support** - Add a `CockroachDB` constant to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`

2. **Configuration Changes** - Create `CockroachDBConfig` in `internal/config/analytics.go` following the ClickHouse pattern

3. **Migration Support** - Create CockroachDB migration files using PostgreSQL-compatible SQL (CockroachDB uses Postgres wire protocol) and update the migrator to use the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver

4. **Configuration Schema Updates** - Add CockroachDB to `config/flipt.schema.cue` 

5. **Testing Infrastructure** - Update `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` to support CockroachDB containers

6. **Server Integration** - Add CockroachDB client initialization in `internal/cmd/grpc.go`

7. **Validation & Tests** - Add configuration tests in `internal/config/analytics_test.go`

**Key Design Decision**: Leverage PostgreSQL as the driver for CockroachDB migrations since CockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, avoiding the need to create a new golang-migrate driver.

The plan is ready for your review. Would you like me to proceed with the implementation following this plan, or do you have any questions or modifications you'd like me to address first?

this suffix.\n//\n// e.g strippedKeys([\"A_B_C_D\", \"A_B_F_D\", \"A_B_E_D_G\"], \"A_B\", \"D\")\n// returns [\"c\", \"f\", \"e\"]\n//\n// It's purpose is to extract the parts of env vars which are likely\n// keys in an arbitrary map type.\nfunc strippedKeys(envs []string, prefix, delim string) (keys []string) {\n\tfor _, env := range envs {\n\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(env, prefix) {\n\t\t\tenv = key and take the left hand component\n\t\t\tif left, _, ok := strings.Cut(env, \"_\"+delim); ok {\n\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, left)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn\n}\n\n// getFliptEnvs returns all environment variables which have FLIPT_\n// as a prefix. It also strips this prefix before appending them to the\n// resulting set.\nfunc getFliptEnvs() (envs []string) {\n\tconst prefix = \"FLIPT_\"\n\tfor _, e := range os.Environ() {\n\t\tkey, _, ok := 158. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# CockroachDB Analytics Backend Implementation Plan\n\n## Context\n\nFlipt currently supports ClickHouse and Prometheus as analytics storage backends, but not CockroachDB despite its PostgreSQL-compatible wire protocol. The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.\n\nCockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.\n\n## Overview\n\nThe implementation involves:\n1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`\n2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`\n3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver\n4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB\n5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n6. Updating testing infrastructure\n7. Integrating CockroachDB into the gRPC server initialization\n\n## Files to Modify\n\n### 1. **Core Driver System** (`internal/storage/analytics/db.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDB` constant to the `Driver` type\n- Update `stringToDriver` map to include `\"cockroachdb\": CockroachDB`\n- Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB configuration\n- Import PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB connections\n\n### 2. **Configuration** (`internal/config/analytics.go`)\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` struct with `Enabled` and `URL` fields\n- Add `CockroachDBConfig` field to `AnalyticsStorageConfig`\n- Add `Options()` method to `CockroachDBConfig` (parse PostgreSQL DSN)\n- Update `String()` method to return \"cockroachdb\" when enabled\n- Update `setDefaults()` to set default values for CockroachDB config\n- Update `validate()` method to validate CockroachDB URL and buffer settings\n- Update `Enabled()` method to check CockroachDB enabled status\n\n### 3. **Migration System** (`internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go`)\n- Import PostgreSQL migration driver from golang-migrate\n- Update `expectedVersions` map to add `CockroachDB: 3`\n- Update `NewMigrator()` function to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL driver\n- Use PostgreSQL migration driver instance for CockroachDB\n\n### 4. **Migration Files** (`internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`)\nCreate three pairs of up/down migration files:\n- `001_create_table_counter_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Analytics table with PostgreSQL-compatible schema\n- `002_create_table_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - Aggregated analytics table\n- `003_create_view_counter_aggregated_analytics.{up,down}.sql` - View for aggregated data\n\nUse standard PostgreSQL DDL syntax (no MergeTree, Enum, or ClickHouse-specific features).\n\n### 5. **Configuration Schemas**\n- **`config/flipt.schema.cue`**: Add `cockroachdb` section to `#analytics.storage` with `enabled` and `url` fields\n- **`config/flipt.schema.json`**: Will be regenerated from CUE schema\n\n### 6. **Testing Infrastructure** (`internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go`)\n- Update `Open()` function to detect and support both ClickHouse and CockroachDB based on environment or config\n- Add CockroachDB container setup function (similar to ClickHouse)\n- Update `newMigrator()` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n- Support both database types in test setup\n\n### 7. **Server Initialization** (`internal/cmd/grpc.go`)\n- Add conditional branch for CockroachDB in analytics initialization\n- Import CockroachDB client (will be created from ClickHouse pattern)\n- Initialize CockroachDB client when enabled in config\n- Register with analytics server\n\n### 8. **Configuration Tests** (`internal/config/analytics_test.go`)\n- Add `TestAnalyticsCockroachDBConfiguration()` test\n- Verify CockroachDB config parsing\n- Test validation logic\n\n### 9. **CockroachDB Client** (`internal/server/analytics/`)\n- Can initially reuse/adapt existing ClickHouse client or create new package\n- Implement methods for flag evaluation counting using PostgreSQL SQL syntax\n- Handle time-series aggregation with PostgreSQL functions\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Core Infrastructure\n1. Add `CockroachDB` to `Driver` type and `stringToDriver` map in `db.go`\n2. Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB connections using PostgreSQL driver\n3. Add CockroachDB configuration to `analytics.go`\n4. Create CockroachDB migration files under `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`\n\n### Phase 2: Migration & Validation\n1. Update `migrator.go` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n2. Add expected version for CockroachDB migrations\n3. Update configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n4. Add configuration validation tests\n\n### Phase 3: Testing & Integration\n1. Update testing infrastructure to support CockroachDB\n2. Add CockroachDB client package (adapt from ClickHouse)\n3. Update server initialization code\n4. Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n",

View for aggregated data\n\nUse standard PostgreSQL DDL syntax (no MergeTree, Enum, or ClickHouse-specific features).\n\n### 5. **Configuration Schemas**\n- **`config/flipt.schema.cue`**: Add `cockroachdb` section to `#analytics.storage` with `enabled` and `url` fields\n- **`config/flipt.schema.json`**: Will be regenerated from CUE schema\n\n### 6. **Testing Infrastructure** (`internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go`)\n- Update `Open()` function to detect and support both ClickHouse and CockroachDB based on environment or config\n- Add CockroachDB container setup function (similar to ClickHouse)\n- Update `newMigrator()` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n- Support both database types in test setup\n\n### 7. **Server Initialization** (`internal/cmd/grpc.go`)\n- Add conditional branch for CockroachDB in analytics initialization\n- Import CockroachDB client (will be created from ClickHouse pattern)\n- Initialize CockroachDB client when enabled in config\n- Register with analytics server\n\n### 8. **Configuration Tests** (`internal/config/analytics_test.go`)\n- Add `TestAnalyticsCockroachDBConfiguration()` test\n- Verify CockroachDB config parsing\n- Test validation logic\n\n### 9. **CockroachDB Client** (`internal/server/analytics/`)\n- Can initially reuse/adapt existing ClickHouse client or create new package\n- Implement methods for flag evaluation counting using PostgreSQL SQL syntax\n- Handle time-series aggregation with PostgreSQL functions\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### Phase 1: Core Infrastructure\n1. Add `CockroachDB` to `Driver` type and `stringToDriver` map in `db.go`\n2. Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB connections using PostgreSQL driver\n3. Add CockroachDB configuration to `analytics.go`\n4. Create CockroachDB migration files under `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/`\n\n### Phase 2: Migration & Validation\n1. Update `migrator.go` to handle CockroachDB with PostgreSQL migration driver\n2. Add expected version for CockroachDB migrations\n3. Update configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)\n4. Add configuration validation tests\n\n### Phase 3: Testing & Integration\n1. Update testing infrastructure to support CockroachDB\n2. Add CockroachDB client package (adapt from ClickHouse)\n3. Update server initialization code\n4. Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n"
}

Verify all tests pass\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Use PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB**: Since CockroachDB is PostgreSQL-compatible, we use the `golang-migrate` PostgreSQL driver instead of creating a new one.\n\n2. **Reuse configuration pattern**: Follow the exact pattern used by ClickHouse configuration to ensure consistency.\n\n3. **Create separate migration files**: Use PostgreSQL-compatible SQL instead of sharing ClickHouse migrations, for clarity and to avoid confusion about schema differences.\n\n4. **Keep analytics client separate**: Potentially reuse or adapt ClickHouse client code, but maintain separation of concerns.\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Test that CockroachDB config is properly loaded from YAML\n2. **Driver Selection**: Verify `open()` function correctly selects CockroachDB when configured\n3. **Migrations**: Run migrations against CockroachDB and verify schema\n4. **Tests**: Run existing test suite to ensure no regressions\n5. **Integration**: Verify CockroachDB client initialization in gRPC server\n6. **End-to-end**: Set up CockroachDB instance and verify analytics collection works\n\n## Potential Challenges\n\n1. **SQL Query Differences**: ClickHouse has unique time-series features; CockroachDB/PostgreSQL equivalents may differ\n2. **Time-series Aggregation**: Need to implement using PostgreSQL window functions instead of ClickHouse's native bucketing\n3. **Data Type Mapping**: Ensure proper mapping between analytics data types and PostgreSQL types\n4. **Migration Compatibility**: CockroachDB may have subtle differences from pure PostgreSQL\n\n## Files Modified Summary\n\n- `internal/storage/analytics/db.go` - Add CockroachDB driver\n- `internal/config/analytics.go` - Add CockroachDB config\n- `internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go` - Add CockroachDB migration support\n- `config/flipt.schema.cue` - Add CockroachDB schema\n- `internal/server/analytics/testing/testing.go` - Add CockroachDB test support\n- `internal/cmd/grpc.go` - Add CockroachDB initialization\n- `internal/config/analytics_test.go` - Add CockroachDB config tests\n- Create `internal/migrations/cockroachdb/*.sql` - Migration files\n- Create or adapt `internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/` - CockroachDB client package\n"

1. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/plans/indexed-dancing-abelson.md
# CockroachDB Analytics Backend Implementation Plan

## Context

Flipt currently supports ClickHouse and Prometheus as analytics storage backends, but not CockroachDB despite its PostgreSQL-compatible wire protocol. The task is to add CockroachDB as a first-class analytics database backend alongside ClickHouse.

CockroachDB uses the PostgreSQL wire protocol, so we can reuse the PostgreSQL golang-migrate driver for migrations. The implementation should follow the existing ClickHouse pattern for consistency.

## Overview

The implementation involves:
1. Adding CockroachDB to the Driver type system in `internal/storage/analytics/db.go`
2. Creating CockroachDB configuration option in `internal/config/analytics.go`
3. Adding CockroachDB migrations using the PostgreSQL driver
4. Updating the migrator to handle CockroachDB
5. Updating configuration schemas (CUE and JSON)
6. Updating testing infrastructure
7. Integrating CockroachDB into the gRPC server initialization

## Files to Modify

### 1. **Core Driver System** (`internal/storage/analytics/db.go`)
- Add `CockroachDB` constant to the `Driver` type
- Update `stringToDriver` map to include `"cockroachdb": CockroachDB`
- Update `open()` function to handle CockroachDB configuration
- Import PostgreSQL driver for CockroachDB connections

### 2. **Configuration** (`internal/config/analytics.go`)
- Add `CockroachDBConfig` struct with `Enabled` and `URL` fields
- Add `CockroachDBConfig` field to `AnalyticsStorageConfig`
- Add `Options()` method to `CockroachDBConfig` (parse PostgreSQL DSN)
- Update `String()` method to return "cockroachdb" when enabled
- Update `setDefaults()` to set default values for CockroachDB config
- Update `validate()` method to validate CockroachDB URL and buffer settings
- Update `Enabled()` method to ch
... (truncated)
